    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText17353034595326656294" style="display:none">HER FUTURE IS AMBITION.<br />With a will of steel, Polish immigrant Florentyna Rosnovski is indeed Abel’s daughter. She shares with her father a love of America, his ideals, and his dream for the future. But she wants more: to be the first female president.<br />HIS FUTURE IS WEALTH.<br />Golden boy Richard Kane was born into a life of luxury. The scion of a banking magnate he is successful, handsome, and determined to carve his own path in the world―with the woman he loves.<br />BUT THEIR PAST HOLDS A SECRET…<br />With Florentyna’s ultimate goal only a heartbeat away, both are about to discover the shattering price of power as a titanic battle of betrayal and deception reaches out from the past―a blood feud between two generations that threatens to destroy everything Florentyna and Richard have fought to achieve.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is no violence, love is included, but no overt sex. It is about a girl from her birth. I think it should be safe enough, if she can deal with th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is no violence, love is included, but no overt sex. It is about a girl from her birth. I think it should be safe enough, if she can deal with the American political system, it can be quite educational. Nothing to fear, easy to read.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2644121447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2644121447" />
    <a title="peachygirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl"><img alt="peachygirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555561561p2/51435362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2644121447?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="peachygirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="peachygirl" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl">peachygirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11533353-the-prodigal-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2644121447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7335575237447140975">Definitely not as great as the first book, but a decent read. <br/>Some parts of the past seemed pointless. It could have been easily more concise without the repetitions from Kane & Abel. Also, the last 100 pages got pretty boring with too many details. <br/>Another major disappointment was Richard not being alive to become the First Gentleman. I loved reading about him more than any other character and it got depressing after that. <br/>Although I have enjoyed these 2 books, I don't think I'll read the next </span>
  <span id="freeText7335575237447140975" style="display:none">Definitely not as great as the first book, but a decent read. <br />Some parts of the past seemed pointless. It could have been easily more concise without the repetitions from Kane &amp; Abel. Also, the last 100 pages got pretty boring with too many details. <br />Another major disappointment was Richard not being alive to become the First Gentleman. I loved reading about him more than any other character and it got depressing after that. <br />Although I have enjoyed these 2 books, I don't think I'll read the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7335575237447140975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_204185674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204185674" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4432628-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288275156p2/4432628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204185674?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/4432628-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204185674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1924634271481300821"><i>The Prodigal Daughter</i> focuses on the life of Florentyna Rosnovski Kane, the daughter of a Polish immigrant who lived the American dream. The first half of this book is a retelling of events from <i>Kane and Abel</i>. The reader gains a few new insights seeing things through Florentyna's eyes, but these were rare because so many passages were completely lifted from the original book and put into this sequel. <br/><br/>One element that seemed to be missing in this book compared to <i>Kane and Abel</i> was the tension and</span>
  <span id="freeText1924634271481300821" style="display:none"><i>The Prodigal Daughter</i> focuses on the life of Florentyna Rosnovski Kane, the daughter of a Polish immigrant who lived the American dream. The first half of this book is a retelling of events from <i>Kane and Abel</i>. The reader gains a few new insights seeing things through Florentyna's eyes, but these were rare because so many passages were completely lifted from the original book and put into this sequel. <br /><br />One element that seemed to be missing in this book compared to <i>Kane and Abel</i> was the tension and plot twists that came about from the bitter feud between the Kane and Rosnovski patriarchs. These two strong wills really made the first book shine, whereas the summary retelling in this book was a bit disappointing. <br /><br />The latter half of the book deals with Florentyna's life in politics. I found this to be rather dry at times, and somewhat predictable as to where Florentyna would eventually end up. If I had read <i>The Prodigal Daughter</i> as a stand-alone book, my review would likely have been higher, but it seemed cheap and lazy to reuse so much material from the first book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1924634271481300821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_138217167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138217167" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2401672-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380476541p2/2401672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138217167?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/2401672-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone with breif knowledge of the American Political system</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138217167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7942736420688841687">Honestly, I found this in my father's car and only popped in the first tape to have something to listen to on my 20 minutes drive to school. I was surprised to find myself engrossed in the novel about a young girl who was the daughter of a Polish immigrant who build his own American Deam in the form of the Baron hotels. Imagine my surprise in finding out that this was the sequel to another best seller, that I will be sure to pick up as soon as possible. The best part was the main character, Flor</span>
  <span id="freeText7942736420688841687" style="display:none">Honestly, I found this in my father's car and only popped in the first tape to have something to listen to on my 20 minutes drive to school. I was surprised to find myself engrossed in the novel about a young girl who was the daughter of a Polish immigrant who build his own American Deam in the form of the Baron hotels. Imagine my surprise in finding out that this was the sequel to another best seller, that I will be sure to pick up as soon as possible. The best part was the main character, Florentyna, and her unwavering honesty and diligence in not only her buisness life but also her politics. I found myself cursing the American political system at times for the unfairness in campaigning schemes and was heartbroken every time Florentyna was hit by a blow from the media during her efforts to make it into the political spotlight. I feel as if her character were a real person, she would be one of the only politicians I would admire. One thing I also loved was how the love story in the book did not take up a major amount of the reader's time, and rather was put in to help push the plot forward and added to the realness of the main character. Not only were the characters wonderful, but the historical facts in the book were added with subtlety and grace. I never knew much about the Polish and found myself engrossed in the telling of the Polish heritage from Florentyna's father. The connection to American politics throughout the whole book taught me more about the history of modern America than I could have ever learned in one of my college classes, all while intertwining it with the lives of the characters. <br /><br />I would reccomend this book to anyone who has knowledge of the American political system and likes fast paced historical fiction with empowering women as lead characters.<br /><br />The only thing about this book is if it were not for my recent class on Mass and the Federal System, I would have been completly lost in the political details of the book. Thankfully I learned what the Majority and Minority leaders, whips, and other political positions held in Congress. That would be my only warning for anyone who decided to read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7942736420688841687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The plot is well-written, though there were some parts that I don't like, but overall, I love this book.<br/><br/>Florentyna was a strong woman. She run her father's hotel empire.   <span id="freeText11016038966923780999" style="display:none">I must have read this book more than 5 times! I was hooked from the beginning til the end. The plot is well-written, though there were some parts that I don't like, but overall, I love this book.<br /><br />Florentyna was a strong woman. She run her father's hotel empire. She was a politician. She had everything that she could ask for yet she also had trials in her life that she must overcome. Though she was raised with golden spoon in her mouth, she wasn't a spoiled brat. When she was dealt with the biggest blow in her pampered life, she had a hard time dealing with it but just like the phoenix, she rose from the ashes.<br /><br />From her triumphs as a student to the White House, this is a very compelling story of a woman who, despite having it all, still suffered from the trials that came her way and how she rose from it all.<br /><br />A very good book!</span>

  <span id="freeText17560646343655704171" style="display:none">The storyline fell apart in the middle and I practically forced myself to complete it- desperately hoping things would take a turn for the better. Unfortunately it did not. Mr Archer's love for politics makes for an interesting window into that world and yet again, as in the case of Kane and Abel, I did not connect with the characters. I do believe that he is a good writer and I may give any of his other books a chance... if anyone has a good recommendation. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3508471512" />
    <a title="Su Mon  Myo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19972495-su-mon-myo"><img alt="Su Mon  Myo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532757610p2/19972495.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3508471512?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Su Mon  Myo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Su Mon  Myo" href="/user/show/19972495-su-mon-myo">Su Mon  Myo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3508471512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17060887269590305839">I picked up Kane and Abel by Jeffrey Archer a few years back. I remembered the writing and the storyline is well-written and the plot is interesting that would take you to the end of the book with a breeze. So, I managed to pick up The Prodigal Daughter, the sequel of Kane and Abel, a couple of days back after reading half way through last time. It has been on my bookshelf forever. <br/><br/>The story follows Florentyna Rosnovski Kane, the daughter of Abel Rosnovski from her birth to becoming The Presiden</span>
  <span id="freeText17060887269590305839" style="display:none">I picked up Kane and Abel by Jeffrey Archer a few years back. I remembered the writing and the storyline is well-written and the plot is interesting that would take you to the end of the book with a breeze. So, I managed to pick up The Prodigal Daughter, the sequel of Kane and Abel, a couple of days back after reading half way through last time. It has been on my bookshelf forever. <br /><br />The story follows Florentyna Rosnovski Kane, the daughter of Abel Rosnovski from her birth to becoming The President of United States. The first part of the book is filled with summaries from Kane and Abel. Abel Rosnovski is a Polish immigrant, who is living American Dream by building a group of hotels named the Baron around the world. <br /><br />The development of character of Florentyna is interesting and well writte. Her love and family life with Richard Kane is a touch and go. The last third of the book follows the journey of Florentyna political career. It is a fast paced book and recommended to anyone who is looking for empowering women character with a flair of American Political System.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17060887269590305839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_336655703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336655703" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3358904-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362536285p2/3358904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336655703?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/3358904-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780671456856" href="/book/show/1996310.The_Prodigal_Daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3358904-mike?shelf=used-paperback">used-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336655703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11507464927310075759">I finished this one last night but I honestly needed a day (and a few drinks) to ponder this recap. <br/><br/>I think it is best for me to research just WHY this novel was even written. Perhaps as a favor to a friend or publisher? There was just no room for story here. So the author instead seemed to toss the plot out the window and use this book to display his knowledge of political inner workings and his ability to be employed as a speech writer. <br/><br/>Had this been a standalone I likely wouldn't have been so</span>
  <span id="freeText11507464927310075759" style="display:none">I finished this one last night but I honestly needed a day (and a few drinks) to ponder this recap. <br /><br />I think it is best for me to research just WHY this novel was even written. Perhaps as a favor to a friend or publisher? There was just no room for story here. So the author instead seemed to toss the plot out the window and use this book to display his knowledge of political inner workings and his ability to be employed as a speech writer. <br /><br />Had this been a standalone I likely wouldn't have been so disappointed. I wouldn't have finished the novel at all! But after such a page turner its predecessor, the bar was set too high to continue. <br /><br />Florentyna is nothing special yet things seem to constantly just work out in her favor. She's smart yes but this isn't a rags to riches story. Making it unrelateable. Making it more fiction than fiction. <br /><br />I didn't mind the recaps and crossed timelines from the first book. Since I don't read series back-to-back, this was a big refresher-help. <br /><br />But what happened to the formula used in KANE &amp; ABEL? There wasn't a single constant struggle or threat or adversary. And nothing was a surprise. It's almost as if this were written by a different author. .</span>
  <a data-text-id="11507464927310075759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

If you loved Kane and Abel for the fierceness of the characters, for the love and die-hard hatred they have for each other, The Prodigal Daughter will go on to tell how the qualities of each of those characters were deeply ingrained in their children to reach and achieve great heights in their lives!<br/><br/>A totally must-read for people that love fast-paced fiction :)<br/><br/>I loved it!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3199282715" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3199282715?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/56446521-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780006478690" href="/book/show/1949808.The_Prodigal_Daughter">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199282715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16464345239237313306">This book was interesting - its nothing like Kane and Abel even thought for the first half of the book or so it covers the same story, although now also from Florentyna's perspective. Although I was a little hesitant at first I grew to really love Florentyna as a main character. Her drive at times was even motivating and her struggles, especially those during her highschool & college years, were much more relateable to me than anything that ever happened between Kane and Abel. I was also surpris</span>
  <span id="freeText16464345239237313306" style="display:none">This book was interesting - its nothing like Kane and Abel even thought for the first half of the book or so it covers the same story, although now also from Florentyna's perspective. Although I was a little hesitant at first I grew to really love Florentyna as a main character. Her drive at times was even motivating and her struggles, especially those during her highschool &amp; college years, were much more relateable to me than anything that ever happened between Kane and Abel. I was also surprised to find how much I enjoyed reading from Richards perspective as well. I like Archer's writing style in general, in a way its comparable to other authors I've read like Dan Brown in the way you are just compelled to keep reading. I will say I was surprised by how feminist this book was at times(especially considering when it was written) but at the same time it also screamed unrecognized privilege. This is also one of my main gripes with the book, that even though Florentyna has some hardships to overcome, and by no means am I saying she had it easy, she never really gets how privileged she is, and even when its discussed its only in terms of "how this might cost me voters" way. I will say that she does try to do a lot of good, but all throughout her journey to try to become President of the US she never really seems ro reflect on any of this..... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and even the way she finally did become president didn't feel right, like just randomly kill of the previous president so that she can gain power, that just seems almost disrespectful to the amount of work she had to do to get there, I would've much preferred it if she was actually voted into presidency, not just accidentally made president because the other guy died of a heart attack  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16464345239237313306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818238339?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9781509808700" href="/book/show/36222641-the-prodigal-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48359311-nour-wanace?shelf=female-led">female-led</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48359311-nour-wanace?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48359311-nour-wanace?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818238339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9837287043456708138">What a book! Super refreshing to read after enjoying a slew of fantastical and/or thrilling murder books. I actually thoroughly enjoyed this, despite not reading the first novel of this series.<br/><br/>The story did a great job of recounting the events of the previous book while introducing the premise for this sequel. I am so absolutely obsessed with Florentyna Rosnovski's bold, spirited and ambitious character. Her defiance of conventions, her witty remarks, her strong demeanor: everything about her ch</span>
  <span id="freeText9837287043456708138" style="display:none">What a book! Super refreshing to read after enjoying a slew of fantastical and/or thrilling murder books. I actually thoroughly enjoyed this, despite not reading the first novel of this series.<br /><br />The story did a great job of recounting the events of the previous book while introducing the premise for this sequel. I am so absolutely obsessed with Florentyna Rosnovski's bold, spirited and ambitious character. Her defiance of conventions, her witty remarks, her strong demeanor: everything about her character was written beautifully! I salute Jeffrey Archer.<br /><br />The story felt like a conversation between the author, Archer swiftly and smoothly told me the story of a great woman, spanning over 60 years, from her childhood and through all highlights of her adulthood, while she pursued her greatest dreams. The book felt like a biography told from the third person. Florentyna's life was full of ups and downs, intrigue and pure diligence and determination on the part of our main character. I found myself going through the same set of emotions as Florentyna: anger, determined willpower, happiness, sorrow and everything in between.<br /><br />My only disappointment was glossing over all the mumbo jumbo about finance and politics, because of my lack of expertise and knowledge in these sections.<br /><br />Florentyna's rise to greatness has been a wild ride, and an inspirational one at that, which made this novel a blast to read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9837287043456708138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6043609394661182414" style="display:none">this is the story of florentyna from 1934 - 1995 <br /><br />the daughter of abel she is grown up adored by her father and the first word she spoke was presidunk, having a teddy bear she called fdr <br /><br />she works and learns hard and is soon putting her influence to her father's hotel group, the baron group <br /><br />but the old rivalry between kane and abel will rear it's ugly head when she falls in love with richard, the former's son <br /><br />needless to say they r thrown out by their respective families and left to cope on their own. this they succeed over the years through fashion shops and banking <br /><br />both kane and abel r long dead and a secret that kane held has been revealed. florentyna now sets off in pursuit of an ambition that dwarfs even theirs - what she mentioned first as a child ...... <br /><br />a well told novel with great characterisation but it was rather drawn out and repetitive in places plus too co-incidental and events obvious were to happen. i liked the middle section best, the present, as it was full of dialogue and the repartee between richard and florentyna certainly struck a spark. the banking intricacies and especially the politics did rather wash over my head and were too encyclopedic for my taste <br /><br />just one question - the name of the preceding president was never mentioned! <br /><br />sorry but the ending did stretch one's credibility somewhat <br /><br />bev </span>

<div id="review_2005300260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2005300260" />
    <a title="Eve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14040411-eve"><img alt="Eve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376582322p2/14040411.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005300260?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eve" href="/user/show/14040411-eve">Eve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14040411-eve?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005300260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16698480409362417854">I love Jeffery Archer books, but I have mixed feelings about The Prodigal Daughter. The first half is typical Archer: I got so immersed in the story that when I finally came up for air, I noticed I had read 200 pages. It's Archer at his best, weaving a family saga made up of rich characters with complicated relationships. <br/><br/>It is worth noting that the first half covers much of the same time frame as Kane & Abel (first novel in the trilogy), but from a different perspective and with new information</span>
  <span id="freeText16698480409362417854" style="display:none">I love Jeffery Archer books, but I have mixed feelings about The Prodigal Daughter. The first half is typical Archer: I got so immersed in the story that when I finally came up for air, I noticed I had read 200 pages. It's Archer at his best, weaving a family saga made up of rich characters with complicated relationships. <br /><br />It is worth noting that the first half covers much of the same time frame as Kane &amp; Abel (first novel in the trilogy), but from a different perspective and with new information. It may be annoying to some, but I thought it was interesting to revisit the story through different eyes. <br /><br />The second half of the novel was somewhat disappointing (impossible, I know!). I won't go into detail so as not to spoil anything, but let's just say that it's mostly a "she did this and she did that." <br /><br />The Prodigal Daughter remains a must-read for those who read and enjoyed Kane &amp; Abel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16698480409362417854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/403571415?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ernest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ernest" href="/user/show/5887368-ernest">Ernest</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780006478690" href="/book/show/1949808.The_Prodigal_Daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5887368-ernest?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403571415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17321444957731233884">Charting the life of Florentyna Kane, Archer is well within his writing element in crafting a story that is both interest and engaging. A standalone sequel of sorts to Kane and Abel, the feud first presented there here is largely a canvas for Florentyna’s life to play out on (rather than being the central narrative thrust of the book). Some may prefer a greater clash between characters or wished for the story or writing to be something much sharper and acerbic, but there is a deftness in how Arc</span>
  <span id="freeText17321444957731233884" style="display:none">Charting the life of Florentyna Kane, Archer is well within his writing element in crafting a story that is both interest and engaging. A standalone sequel of sorts to Kane and Abel, the feud first presented there here is largely a canvas for Florentyna’s life to play out on (rather than being the central narrative thrust of the book). Some may prefer a greater clash between characters or wished for the story or writing to be something much sharper and acerbic, but there is a deftness in how Archer weaves power, politics, and profit (including into and amongst real events) to produce a story that I was most interested in reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17321444957731233884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mJ+0r3odsKZiCr1jf+oHnKsk+3pCHB/7XEHNRzogFvoH2bQEAKfTsht+lncnoDXdG9Iono4fliZLA2nimg74iQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6f6Hs2/nVYgHNL6umFY66vb8eh3c44gp2PA7YN7N99B2uIcYFV02nH5AlbrAHAirRgqp+RDgAfTPsp/FfuMZow==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7512230573514203661">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br/><br/>He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married </span>
  <span id="freeText7512230573514203661" style="display:none">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br /><br />He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married to Mary Archer, a scientist specialising in solar power. Outside politics, he is a novelist, playwright and short story writer.<br /><br /><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Archer" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia link</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffreyarcher">http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffre...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7512230573514203661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
